	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Kristin Chenoweth</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div class="fn" style="display:inline">Kristin /></a><div>Chenoweth in 2018</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td><div style="display:inline" class="nickname">Kristi Dawn Chenoweth</div><br /><span style="display:none"> (<span career</b></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Genres</th><td><div class="hlist hlist-separated"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">Musical theatre</a></li><li><a />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kristin Dawn Chenoweth</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/tʃ/: &#39;ch&#39; in &#39;China&#39;">tʃ</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="/θ/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">θ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born <b>Kristi Dawn Chenoweth</b>, July 24, 1968)<sup id="cite_ref-biochannel_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biochannel-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> is an American actress and singer, with credits in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>, film and television. In 1999, she won a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Featured_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Featured Actress in a Musical">Tony Award</a> for her performance as <a href="/wiki/Sally_Brown" title="Sally Brown">Sally Brown</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/You%27re_a_Good_Man,_Charlie_Brown" title="You&#39;re a Good Man, Charlie Brown">You're a Good Man, Charlie Brown</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a>. In 2003, she received wide notice for originating the role of <a href="/wiki/Glinda" class="mw-redirect" title="Glinda">Glinda</a> in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_(musical)" title="Wicked (musical)">Wicked</a></i>, including a nomination for another Tony.  Her television roles have included <a href="/wiki/Annabeth_Schott" title="Annabeth Schott">Annabeth Schott</a> in NBC's <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Olive_Snook" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive Snook">Olive Snook</a> on the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy-drama" title="Comedy-drama">comedy-drama</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pushing_Daisies" title="Pushing Daisies">Pushing Daisies</a></i>, for which she won a 2009 <a href="/wiki/61st_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="61st Primetime Emmy Awards">Emmy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actress_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series">Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series</a>. Chenoweth also starred in the ABC TV series <i><a href="/wiki/GCB_(TV_series)" title="GCB (TV series)">GCB</a></i> in 2012.
</p><p>Chenoweth sang <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel music</a> as a child in <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> and studied <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> before deciding to pursue a career in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>. In 1997, she made her Broadway debut in <i><a href="/wiki/Steel_Pier_(musical)" title="Steel Pier (musical)">Steel Pier</a></i>, winning a <a href="/wiki/Theatre_World_Award" title="Theatre World Award">Theatre World Award</a>.  Besides <i>You're a Good Man, Charlie Brown</i> and <i>Wicked</i>, Chenoweth's stage work includes five City Center <a href="/wiki/Encores!" title="Encores!">Encores!</a> productions, Broadway's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apple_Tree" title="The Apple Tree">The Apple Tree</a></i> in 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Promises,_Promises_(musical)" title="Promises, Promises (musical)">Promises, Promises</a></i> in 2010 and <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Twentieth_Century" title="On the Twentieth Century">On the Twentieth Century</a></i> in 2015, as well as <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">Off-Broadway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_theater_in_the_United_States" title="Regional theater in the United States">regional theatre</a> productions.
</p><p>Chenoweth had her own sitcom, <i><a href="/wiki/Kristin_(TV_series)" title="Kristin (TV series)">Kristin</a></i>, in 2001, and has guest-starred on many shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/Sesame_Street" title="Sesame Street">Sesame Street</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>, for which she was nominated for Emmy Awards in 2010 and 2011. In films, she has played mostly character roles, such as in <i><a href="/wiki/Bewitched_(2005_film)" title="Bewitched (2005 film)">Bewitched</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pink_Panther_(2006_film)" title="The Pink Panther (2006 film)">The Pink Panther</a></i> (2006) and <i><a href="/wiki/RV_(film)" title="RV (film)">RV</a></i> (2006). She has played roles in made-for-TV movies, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Descendants_(2015_film)" title="Descendants (2015 film)">Descendants</a></i> (2015); done voice work in animated films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Rio_2" title="Rio 2">Rio 2</a></i> (2014) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Peanuts_Movie" title="The Peanuts Movie">The Peanuts Movie</a></i> (2015) along with the animated TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Sit_Down,_Shut_Up_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sit Down, Shut Up (U.S. TV series)">Sit Down, Shut Up</a></i>; hosted several award shows; and released several albums of songs, including <i><a href="/wiki/A_Lovely_Way_to_Spend_Christmas" title="A Lovely Way to Spend Christmas">A Lovely Way to Spend Christmas</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Lessons_Learned" title="Some Lessons Learned">Some Lessons Learned</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Coming_Home_(Kristin_Chenoweth_album)" title="Coming Home (Kristin Chenoweth album)">Coming Home</a></i> (2014) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Elegance" title="The Art of Elegance">The Art of Elegance</a></i> (2016). Chenoweth also penned a 2009 memoir, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Bit_Wicked" title="A Little Bit Wicked">A Little Bit Wicked</a></i>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Chenoweth was adopted when she was five days old by Junie Smith Chenoweth and Jerry Morris Chenoweth, both <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical engineers</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Broken_Arrow,_Oklahoma" title="Broken Arrow, Oklahoma">Broken Arrow, Oklahoma</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Tulsa,_Oklahoma" title="Tulsa, Oklahoma">Tulsa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and named Kristi Dawn Chenoweth.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> She has stated that she is of one quarter <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">Cherokee</a> ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> At an early age, she performed gospel songs for local churches. A performing highlight of her childhood was a solo appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> national conference at the age of 12, where she performed the <a href="/wiki/Evie_(singer)" title="Evie (singer)">Evie</a> song "Four Feet Eleven". The chorus begins, "I'm only 4 feet 11, but I'm going to Heaven" (Chenoweth is 4&#160;ft 11&#160;in (150&#160;cm) in height).<sup id="cite_ref-tcm_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> After graduating from <a href="/wiki/Broken_Arrow_Senior_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Broken Arrow Senior High School">Broken Arrow Senior High School</a>, where she participated in school plays, Chenoweth attended <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City_University" title="Oklahoma City University">Oklahoma City University</a>, where she was a member of <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a> (Beta Omicron) sorority.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She earned a bachelor's degree in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a> in 1990<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allen_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and a master's degree in opera performance in 1992,<sup id="cite_ref-Allen_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> studying under voice instructor and mentor, <a href="/wiki/Florence_Birdwell" title="Florence Birdwell">Florence Birdwell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-okcu_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-okcu-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> While at OCU, Chenoweth competed in beauty pageants, winning the title of "Miss OCU" and was the second runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/Miss_Oklahoma" title="Miss Oklahoma">Miss Oklahoma</a> pageant in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-tcm_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, Chenoweth participated in a studio recording of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Most_Happy_Fella" title="The Most Happy Fella">The Most Happy Fella</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kristinofficial_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristinofficial-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While she was in college and working towards her masters, Chenoweth performed at the Lyric Theatre in <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a>, among other <a href="/wiki/Regional_theater_in_the_United_States" title="Regional theater in the United States">regional theatres</a>, in roles like June in <i><a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(musical)" title="Gypsy (musical)">Gypsy</a></i>, Liesl in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music" title="The Sound of Music">The Sound of Music</a></i>, Fran in <i><a href="/wiki/Promises,_Promises_(musical)" title="Promises, Promises (musical)">Promises, Promises</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and Tuptim in <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_and_I" title="The King and I">The King and I</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> As she completed her master's degree, Chenoweth participated in a number of vocal competitions and was named "most promising up-and-coming singer" in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">Metropolitan Opera</a> National Council auditions, which came with a full scholarship to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Vocal_Arts" title="Academy of Vocal Arts">Academy of Vocal Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Culwell_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culwell-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Two weeks before school started, however, she went to New York City to help a friend move. While there, she auditioned for the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Paper_Mill_Playhouse" title="Paper Mill Playhouse">Paper Mill Playhouse</a> production of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_Crackers_(musical)" title="Animal Crackers (musical)">Animal Crackers</a></i> and got the role of Arabella Rittenhouse. She turned down the scholarship and moved to New York to do the show and pursue a career in musical theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-Culwell_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culwell-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodWalk_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodWalk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <i>Animal Crackers</i>, Chenoweth continued to appear in <a href="/wiki/Regional_theater_in_the_United_States" title="Regional theater in the United States">regional theatre</a> productions, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Babes_in_Arms" title="Babes in Arms">Babes in Arms</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/The_Guthrie_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guthrie Theater">The Guthrie Theater</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Phantom_(musical)" title="Phantom (musical)">Phantom</a></i> (as Christine; also touring in Germany in this role),<sup id="cite_ref-filmreference_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmreference-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> also taking roles in <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">Off-Broadway</a> productions like Luisa in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fantasticks" title="The Fantasticks">The Fantasticks</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-tcm_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie2014_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie2014-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and Kristy in <i>Box Office of the Damned</i> (both in 1994).<sup id="cite_ref-filmreference_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmreference-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, she appeared as Hyacinth in the <a href="/wiki/Roundabout_Theater_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Roundabout Theater Company">Roundabout Theater Company</a> production of <a href="/wiki/Moliere" class="mw-redirect" title="Moliere">Moliere</a>'s farcical <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Fourberies_de_Scapin" class="mw-redirect" title="Les Fourberies de Scapin">Scapin</a></i>, earning her first <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> review, with <a href="/wiki/Ben_Brantley" title="Ben Brantley">Ben Brantley</a> writing "Kristin Chenoweth's sob-prone ingenue&#160;... [is] delightful".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> She made her <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> debut in the spring of 1997 as Precious McGuire in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Steel_Pier_(musical)" title="Steel Pier (musical)">Steel Pier</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Kander_and_Ebb" title="Kander and Ebb">Kander and Ebb</a>, for which she won a <a href="/wiki/Theatre_World_Award" title="Theatre World Award">Theatre World Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tcm_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>  In 1998 she appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Encores!" title="Encores!">City Center Encores!</a> staged concert of the <a href="/wiki/George_Gershwin" title="George Gershwin">George</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ira_Gershwin" title="Ira Gershwin">Ira Gershwin</a> musical <i><a href="/wiki/Strike_up_the_Band_(musical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strike up the Band (musical)">Strike up the Band</a></i> as Anne Draper<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and created roles in the original <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln Center Theater">Lincoln Center Theater</a> production of <a href="/wiki/William_Finn" title="William Finn">William Finn</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_New_Brain" title="A New Brain">A New Brain</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rimalower" title="Ben Rimalower">Ben Rimalower</a>, in <i>Playbill</i>, wrote: "It's unlikely anyone will equal Kristin Chenoweth in the role of 'Nancy D., the waitress.'"<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Laura_Bush,_Kristin_Chenoweth,_and_models.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Laura_Bush%2C_Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_and_models.jpg/300px-Laura_Bush%2C_Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_and_models.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Laura_Bush%2C_Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_and_models.jpg/450px-Laura_Bush%2C_Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_and_models.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Laura_Bush%2C_Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_and_models.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="343" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Laura_Bush,_Kristin_Chenoweth,_and_models.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chenoweth (holding her dog, Madeline Kahn "Maddie" Chenoweth) with <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a> and celebrity models in the 2007 Red Dress Collection Celebrity Fashion Show to raise awareness of heart disease</div></div></div>
<p>In 1999, Chenoweth performed in the Broadway revival of <i><a href="/wiki/You%27re_a_Good_Man,_Charlie_Brown" title="You&#39;re a Good Man, Charlie Brown">You're a Good Man, Charlie Brown</a></i> as the title character's little sister, <a href="/wiki/Sally_Brown" title="Sally Brown">Sally</a>, a character that was not present in the original production.  She won the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk</a> awards for Best Featured Actress in a Musical.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, she starred on Broadway in the short-lived comic play <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_Proportions" title="Epic Proportions">Epic Proportions</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> followed by starring as Daisy Gamble in the "Encores!" production of <i><a href="/wiki/On_a_Clear_Day_You_Can_See_Forever" title="On a Clear Day You Can See Forever">On a Clear Day You Can See Forever</a></i> in <span class="nowrap">February 2000</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After this, Chenoweth split her time between stage and TV or film roles and released her first solo album, <i>Let Yourself Go</i> (2001). In 2002, she performed in the City Center Encores! <i>10th Anniversary Bash</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In October&#160; 2003, she returned to Broadway (after the San Francisco tryout) in <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_(musical)" title="Wicked (musical)">Wicked</a></i>, the musical about the early years of the witches of <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Oz" title="Land of Oz">Oz</a>, in the joint-leading role of <a href="/wiki/Glinda" class="mw-redirect" title="Glinda">Glinda</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Good_Witch_of_the_North" title="Good Witch of the North">Good Witch of the North</a>.  She was nominated for a 2004 Tony Award as <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Leading_Actress_in_a_Musical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tony Award for Best Leading Actress in a Musical">Best Leading Actress in a Musical</a> for her performance, losing to her co-star <a href="/wiki/Idina_Menzel" title="Idina Menzel">Idina Menzel</a> (who played <a href="/wiki/Elphaba" title="Elphaba">Elphaba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wicked_Witch_of_the_West" title="Wicked Witch of the West">Wicked Witch of the West</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth was also nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Drama_League_Award" title="Drama League Award">Drama League Award</a> for this role.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Ben Rimalower, in <i>Playbill</i>, wrote that, for Glinda, "the gold standard was unquestionably and indelibly set" by Chenoweth's performances.<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> After playing Glinda for nine months, Chenoweth left <i>Wicked</i>, on <span class="nowrap">July 18</span>, 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> soon joining the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i> in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-Culwell_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culwell-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Wicked</i> cast album earned a 2005 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth played <a href="/wiki/Cunegonde" class="mw-redirect" title="Cunegonde">Cunegonde</a> in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Philharmonic" title="New York Philharmonic">New York Philharmonic</a> revival of <i><a href="/wiki/Candide_(musical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Candide (musical)">Candide</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Lonny_Price" title="Lonny Price">Lonny Price</a>, in <span class="nowrap">May 2004</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The production was also broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Performances" title="Great Performances">Great Performances</a></i>. A performance of the rarely sung duet "We Are Women", between Cunegonde and the Old Lady (played by <a href="/wiki/Patti_Lupone" class="mw-redirect" title="Patti Lupone">Patti Lupone</a>), was included in the production.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodWalk_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodWalk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From December 2006 to March 2007, Chenoweth starred on Broadway as Eve in a revival of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apple_Tree" title="The Apple Tree">The Apple Tree</a></i> with co-stars <a href="/wiki/Brian_d%27Arcy_James" title="Brian d&#39;Arcy James">Brian d'Arcy James</a> and former fiancé <a href="/wiki/Marc_Kudisch" title="Marc Kudisch">Marc Kudisch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> She received nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-nom_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nom-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Drama_League_Award" title="Drama League Award">Drama League Award</a>.  She hosted that year's <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Awards</a> ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-nom_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nom-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> She appeared in the Encores! semi-staged production of <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Kern" title="Jerome Kern">Jerome Kern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Hammerstein_II" title="Oscar Hammerstein II">Oscar Hammerstein&#160;II</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Music_in_the_Air" title="Music in the Air">Music in the Air</a></i> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth was scheduled to return to The Metropolitan Opera in 2010 to play Samira in <a href="/wiki/John_Corigliano" title="John Corigliano">John Corigliano</a>'s opera <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ghosts_of_Versailles" title="The Ghosts of Versailles">The Ghosts of Versailles</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The Met cancelled the expensive production in 2008 as the U.S. economy weakened.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth starred as Fran Kubelik in the 2010 Broadway revival of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Promises,_Promises_(musical)" title="Promises, Promises (musical)">Promises, Promises</a></i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Sean_Hayes_(actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Hayes (actor)">Sean Hayes</a>, which opened on <span class="nowrap">April 25</span>, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The songs "<a href="/wiki/I_Say_a_Little_Prayer" title="I Say a Little Prayer">I Say a Little Prayer</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/A_House_Is_Not_a_Home_(song)" title="A House Is Not a Home (song)">A House Is Not a Home</a>" were added for her to sing.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth and Hayes remained in the cast until the show closed on January 2, 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-extend_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extend-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> although she missed performances from December 29, 2010, to January 1, 2011, to perform a New Year's Eve concert at Walt Disney Concert Hall on December 31, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-extend_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extend-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> She played televangelist <a href="/wiki/Tammy_Faye_Bakker" class="mw-redirect" title="Tammy Faye Bakker">Tammy Faye Bakker</a> in a reading of the musical <i>Rise</i> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth played Lily Garland in a Broadway revival of <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Twentieth_Century" title="On the Twentieth Century">On the Twentieth Century</a></i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gallagher" title="Peter Gallagher">Peter Gallagher</a>, which began previews on February 12 and opened on March 12, 2015, for a 22-week limited engagement through July 19, 2015, at the <a href="/wiki/Roundabout_Theatre_Company" title="Roundabout Theatre Company">Roundabout Theatre Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ben_Brantley" title="Ben Brantley">Ben Brantley</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> wrote that Chenoweth "uses [her character's] histrionics to create one of the most virtuosic portraits in song ever on Broadway. The vocal vocabulary she deploys here ranges from jazz-baby brass to operatic silver, often in a single number, and she switches among them with jaw-dropping ease.&#160;...  And every perfectly weighted note is set off by an impeccably exaggerated gesture."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> She was nominated for a Tony Award and won a Drama Desk Award for her performance.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a guest appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/LateLine" title="LateLine">LateLine</a></i>, a role in the short-lived television series <i>Paramour</i> (1999) and several roles in <a href="/wiki/Television_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Television films">television films</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_(1999_film)" title="Annie (1999 film)">Annie</a></i> (as Lily St. Regis), Chenoweth starred in her own <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">sitcom</a>, the semi-autobiographical <i><a href="/wiki/Kristin_(TV_series)" title="Kristin (TV series)">Kristin</a></i> in 2001. It was short-lived, with thirteen episodes filmed, but only six aired before it was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth appeared in the lead role of Marian in the 2003 television film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Music_Man_(2003_film)" title="The Music Man (2003 film)">The Music Man</a></i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Broderick" title="Matthew Broderick">Matthew Broderick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> She also guest-starred on such shows as <i><a href="/wiki/Frasier" title="Frasier">Frasier</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Sesame_Street" title="Sesame Street">Sesame Street</a></i> (2002 and several times afterwards) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ugly_Betty" title="Ugly Betty">Ugly Betty</a></i> (2007).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Chenoweth began playing the recurring role of media consultant <a href="/wiki/Annabeth_Schott" title="Annabeth Schott">Annabeth Schott</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Culwell_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culwell-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> For her performance, she was nominated twice, along with the cast, for a <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award" title="Screen Actors Guild Award">Screen Actors Guild Award</a>. She appeared in the final two seasons of the program, through 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth had been considered originally for the role of <a href="/wiki/Ainsley_Hayes" class="mw-redirect" title="Ainsley Hayes">Ainsley Hayes</a>, but she had already accepted her role in <i>Wicked</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg/220px-Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg/330px-Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg/440px-Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth_-_2012_Drama_League_Benefit_Gala_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chenoweth at the 2012<br /><a href="/wiki/Drama_League_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Drama League of New York">Drama League</a> Benefit Gala</div></div></div>
<p>From 2007 to 2009, Chenoweth played <a href="/wiki/Olive_Snook" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive Snook">Olive Snook</a> in the television series, <i><a href="/wiki/Pushing_Daisies" title="Pushing Daisies">Pushing Daisies</a></i>. For her performance she received critical acclaim and was nominated two years in a row for an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> winning in 2009 as <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actress_%E2%80%93_Comedy_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress – Comedy Series">Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The series was canceled after two seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-tcm_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>  In 2009, Chenoweth lent her voice to the animated comedy series <i><a href="/wiki/Sit_Down,_Shut_Up_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sit Down, Shut Up (U.S. TV series)">Sit Down, Shut Up</a></i> as Miracle Grohe, a science teacher who does not believe in science.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The series lasted just thirteen episodes. Later that year, Chenoweth began a recurring role as <a href="/wiki/April_Rhodes" class="mw-redirect" title="April Rhodes">April Rhodes</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>, singing several songs, earning enthusiastic notices. The character is a former member of the glee club who never finished high school and ended up hitting rock bottom.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> A review in <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> observed, "Her presence may not make much sense, but [if] it means hearing Chenoweth sing, we can put up with any explanation the show cares to offer."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> She received a <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellite Award">Satellite Award</a> for Outstanding Guest Star.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Chenoweth returned to <i>Glee</i> as April Rhodes, singing more songs.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> review commented, "the best part about '<a href="/wiki/Home_(Glee)" title="Home (Glee)">Home</a>' was undoubtedly the return of Kristin Chenoweth as April. ... From her spunky duet of '<a href="/wiki/Fire_(Bruce_Springsteen_song)" title="Fire (Bruce Springsteen song)">Fire</a>' with Schue, to the heart-achingly lonely coo of '<a href="/wiki/One_Less_Bell_to_Answer" title="One Less Bell to Answer">One Less Bell to Answer</a>' which segued into a fantastic reprise of '<a href="/wiki/A_House_Is_Not_a_Home_(song)" title="A House Is Not a Home (song)">A House Is Not a Home</a>' and of course her bone-chilling take on '<a href="/wiki/Home_(The_Wiz_song)" title="Home (The Wiz song)">Home</a>' ... I fell in love with her again."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> She was nominated for both 2010 and 2011 Emmy Awards for her performances on <i>Glee</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth returned again to <i>Glee</i> in "<a href="/wiki/Rumours_(Glee)" title="Rumours (Glee)">Rumours</a>" in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-TVGuideCredits_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVGuideCredits-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and for its 100th episode in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Chenoweth joined the cast of a pilot for <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> called <i>Good Christian Bitches</i> as a character named Carlene Cockburn.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>  ABC picked up the show and changed the title to <i><a href="/wiki/GCB_(TV_series)" title="GCB (TV series)">GCB</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The series debuted in 2012 but lasted only one season; Chenoweth generally sang a song in each episode.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, she guest starred in an episode of the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_in_Cleveland" title="Hot in Cleveland">Hot in Cleveland</a></i>, titled "The Gateway Friend".<sup id="cite_ref-TVGuideCredits_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVGuideCredits-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth played a recurring role as a political reporter in the fourth season of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Wife_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Good Wife (TV series)">The Good Wife</a></i> (2012).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> However, she soon left the show because of serious injuries suffered on the set, where she sustained a skull fracture, broken nose, spinal and rib injuries, and cracked teeth.<sup id="cite_ref-fracture_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fracture-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> She appeared in the 2012 season opener<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and returned in a short scene for another episode.<sup id="cite_ref-short_scene_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-short_scene-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 and 2014, she made two appearances as Brittany Gold on the TV series, <i><a href="/wiki/Kirstie_(TV_series)" title="Kirstie (TV series)">Kirstie</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kirstie_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirstie-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kirstie-return_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirstie-return-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth played <a href="/wiki/Maleficent" title="Maleficent">Maleficent</a> in the live-action <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a> original movie, <i><a href="/wiki/Descendants_(2015_film)" title="Descendants (2015 film)">Descendants</a></i>. The <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> reviewer said that "Chenoweth stole much of the show".<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> It drew the largest cable TV movie audience of 2015 to that date.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> later that year, Chenoweth appeared in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/I_Get_That_a_Lot" title="I Get That a Lot">I Get That a Lot</a></i>, posing as a waitress,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and co-hosted the <i><a href="/wiki/69th_Tony_Awards" title="69th Tony Awards">69th Tony Awards</a></i>, for which she was nominated for another Emmy Award.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth played Velma Von Tussle in NBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Hairspray_Live!" title="Hairspray Live!">Hairspray Live!</a></i> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Hairspray_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hairspray-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Chenoweth played the role of <a href="/wiki/%C4%92ostre" title="Ēostre">Easter</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz</a> TV series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Gods_(TV_series)" title="American Gods (TV series)">American Gods</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 on <i><a href="/wiki/Trial_%26_Error_(TV_series)" title="Trial &amp; Error (TV series)">Trial &amp; Error</a></i> she appeared as Lavinia Peck-Foster, an eccentric heiress accused of her husband's murder, who hires Josh Segal and Associates to defend her.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> She participated in a 2018 NBC broadcast, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Wicked_Halloween" title="A Very Wicked Halloween">A Very Wicked Halloween</a></i>, hosting and singing <i>Popular</i> and other numbers to celebrate the 15th anniversary of <i>Wicked</i> on Broadway.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenker_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenker-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The same year, she appeared as a guest on another NBC special, <i><a href="/wiki/Darci_Lynne" title="Darci Lynne">Darci Lynne</a>: My Hometown Christmas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  In March 2019, Chenoweth appeared on British TV as a judge on an ITV special "All Star Musicals". She and <a href="/wiki/Elaine_Paige" title="Elaine Paige">Elaine Paige</a> also both performed "<a href="/wiki/I_Know_Him_So_Well" title="I Know Him So Well">I Know Him So Well</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chenoweth made her film debut in <i>Topa Topa Bluffs</i> in 2002 playing "Patty".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> After a few years away from film she returned to the big screen in the 2005 film version of <i><a href="/wiki/Bewitched_(2005_film)" title="Bewitched (2005 film)">Bewitched</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Nora_Ephron" title="Nora Ephron">Nora Ephron</a>, as Maria Kelly. In 2006, Chenoweth played supporting roles in five films, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pink_Panther_(2006_film)" title="The Pink Panther (2006 film)">The Pink Panther</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/RV_(film)" title="RV (film)">RV</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Running_with_Scissors_(film)" title="Running with Scissors (film)">Running with Scissors</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Deck_the_Halls_(2006_film)" title="Deck the Halls (2006 film)">Deck the Halls</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Stranger_than_Fiction_(2006_film)" title="Stranger than Fiction (2006 film)">Stranger Than Fiction</a></i>.
</p><p>On February 24, 2008, Chenoweth sang "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_How_You_Know_(musical_number)" class="mw-redirect" title="That&#39;s How You Know (musical number)">That's How You Know</a>" from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Enchanted_(2007_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enchanted (2007 film)">Enchanted</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards" title="80th Academy Awards">80th Academy Awards</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kodak_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodak Theater">Kodak Theater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> She also voiced Rosetta, the garden fairy in the 2008 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Tinker_Bell_(film)" title="Tinker Bell (film)">Tinker Bell</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, Chenoweth appeared in the 2008 holiday <a href="/wiki/Romantic_comedy" title="Romantic comedy">romantic comedy</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Four_Christmases" title="Four Christmases">Four Christmases</a></i>, playing the sister of <a href="/wiki/Reese_Witherspoon" title="Reese Witherspoon">Reese Witherspoon</a>'s character.
</p><p>In 2009, Chenoweth starred as a "suicidal prostitute" in the indie drama <i><a href="/wiki/Into_Temptation_(film)" title="Into Temptation (film)">Into Temptation</a></i>, written and directed by Patrick Coyle. The film was screened at the <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach_Film_Festival" title="Newport Beach Film Festival">Newport Beach Film Festival</a> and was later released on DVD.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  Also in 2009, Chenoweth reprised her voice role of Rosetta in <i><a href="/wiki/Tinker_Bell_and_the_Lost_Treasure" title="Tinker Bell and the Lost Treasure">Tinker Bell and the Lost Treasure</a></i> and filmed the Disney comedy <i><a href="/wiki/You_Again" title="You Again">You Again</a></i> (released in 2010). She voiced Gabi, a poisonous frog, in the 2014 animated film, <i><a href="/wiki/Rio_2" title="Rio 2">Rio 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, she appeared with  <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Guzman" title="Ryan Guzman">Ryan Guzman</a> in the thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boy_Next_Door_(film)" title="The Boy Next Door (film)">The Boy Next Door</a></i> and voiced <a href="/wiki/Fifi_(Peanuts)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fifi (Peanuts)">Fifi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoopy" title="Snoopy">Snoopy</a>'s love interest, in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Peanuts_Movie" title="The Peanuts Movie">The Peanuts Movie</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> She voiced Princess Skystar in the 2017 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_The_Movie_(2017_film)" title="My Little Pony: The Movie (2017 film)">My Little Pony</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and voices Abby the Mouse in the animated movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Star_(2017_film)" title="The Star (2017 film)">The Star</a></i> (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-The_Star_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Star-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media">Other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chenoweth often appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/A_Prairie_Home_Companion" title="A Prairie Home Companion">A Prairie Home Companion</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  On August 27, 2008, Chenoweth released an internet video with <a href="/wiki/Funny_or_Die" title="Funny or Die">Funny or Die</a> called <i>Intervention with Kristin Chenoweth</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-funny_or_die_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-funny_or_die-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The video parodied <a href="/wiki/A%26E_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="A&amp;E Network">A&amp;E</a>'s show <i><a href="/wiki/Intervention_(TV_series)" title="Intervention (TV series)">Intervention</a></i>, with Chenoweth starring as a singing, dancing interventionist. The song in the video was composed by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lippa" title="Andrew Lippa">Andrew Lippa</a>, with lyrics by Amy Rhodes, who also wrote the script for the video.<sup id="cite_ref-funny_or_die_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-funny_or_die-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth admitted that she was hesitant about performing the lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, she appeared in a three-minute video short for <i><a href="/wiki/Glamour_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Glamour Magazine">Glamour Magazine</a></i> entitled "iPad or Bust".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> She posed for the cover and a photo spread in the March 2006 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/FHM" title="FHM">FHM</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>  In 2011, Chenoweth released her first televised music video on <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">Country Music Television</a>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Roman_White" title="Roman White">Roman White</a>, for her song "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_Somebody_(Bitch_About)" title="I Want Somebody (Bitch About)">I Want Somebody</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The video for the single peaked at #19 on <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">CMT</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Top_Twenty_Countdown" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Twenty Countdown">Top Twenty Countdown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recordings_and_concerts">Recordings and concerts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recordings and concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg/220px-Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg/330px-Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg/440px-Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1293" data-file-height="1335" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth_at_the_Oxford_Union_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chenoweth at the Oxford Union, 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Chenoweth has a distinctive speaking voice, one she has compared to that of <a href="/wiki/Betty_Boop" title="Betty Boop">Betty Boop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> She is a classically trained <a href="/wiki/Coloratura_soprano" title="Coloratura soprano">coloratura soprano</a>, able to sing the note "F6" (also known as "F above High C").<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among other early recordings, Chenoweth participated in a studio cast recording of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Most_Happy_Fella" title="The Most Happy Fella">The Most Happy Fella</a></i> in 1992. She was also in the cast recordings of <i>A New Brain</i> (1998) and <i>You're a Good Man, Charlie Brown</i> (1999) and a studio cast recording of <i><a href="/wiki/110_in_the_Shade" title="110 in the Shade">110 in the Shade</a></i> (1999).  In 2000, she was featured on the album <i>Grateful: The Songs of <a href="/wiki/John_Bucchino" title="John Bucchino">John Bucchino</a></i>.  The next year, with Mandy Patinkin, she was featured on the album entitled "Kidults".<sup id="cite_ref-Kristinofficial_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristinofficial-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  Also in 2001, she released her debut solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Let_Yourself_Go_(Kristin_Chenoweth_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Let Yourself Go (Kristin Chenoweth album)">Let Yourself Go</a></i>, which was a collection of standards from the musicals of the 1930s. One of the tracks featured a duet with <a href="/wiki/Jason_Alexander" title="Jason Alexander">Jason Alexander</a>. In <span class="nowrap">October 2002</span>, Chenoweth performed songs from the album in concert for <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln Center">Lincoln Center</a>'s American Songbook concert series.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Ben Rimalower, in <i>Playbill</i>, praised the album as "a joyous affair".<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The same year, she appeared as <a href="/wiki/Fanny_Brice" title="Fanny Brice">Fanny Brice</a> in the Actor's Fund Benefit Concert of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Funny_Girl_(musical)" title="Funny Girl (musical)">Funny Girl</a></i> in New York City.  In 2003 in London, she performed a solo concert as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Divas_at_the_Donmar" title="Divas at the Donmar">Divas at the Donmar</a></i> series for director <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a>.  Later that year, she sang Glinda in the cast recording of <i>Wicked</i> and the soundtrack recording of Disney's <i>The Music Man</i>. Rimalower wrote that Chenoweth "sparkles" on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, she released her second album <i><a href="/wiki/As_I_Am_(Kristin_Chenoweth_album)" title="As I Am (Kristin Chenoweth album)">As I Am</a></i>, which was a Christian music album containing various spiritual songs. The album peaked at number 31 on the U.S. Christian Albums Chart.  The same year, Chenoweth gave a concert at <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Hall" title="Carnegie Hall">Carnegie Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kristinofficial_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristinofficial-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 19, 2007, Chenoweth performed a solo concert at <a href="/wiki/The_Metropolitan_Opera" class="mw-redirect" title="The Metropolitan Opera">The Metropolitan Opera</a> in New York titled <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Chenoweth_Live_At_The_Met" class="mw-redirect" title="Kristin Chenoweth Live At The Met">Kristin Chenoweth Live At The Met</a>, making history as only the third musical theatre star ever to present a solo concert at that location, following <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Cook" title="Barbara Cook">Barbara Cook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yves_Montand" title="Yves Montand">Yves Montand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The same year, she was featured in songs with <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Gunn" title="Nathan Gunn">Nathan Gunn</a> on an album entitled <i>Just Before Sunrise</i>. The next year, she released her third solo studio album, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/A_Lovely_Way_to_Spend_Christmas" title="A Lovely Way to Spend Christmas">A Lovely Way to Spend Christmas</a></i>. The album included a duet with <a href="/wiki/John_Pizzarelli" title="John Pizzarelli">John Pizzarelli</a> and there are several modern holiday tunes, but many traditional carols as well including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord%27s_Prayer" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lord&#39;s Prayer">The Lord's Prayer</a></i>.  This album has been her best seller, reaching number 77 on the U.S. Billboard Albums Chart, climbing to number 7 on the U.S. Holiday Albums chart and to number 1 on the U.S. Heatseekers Chart. Ben Rimalower, in <i>Playbill</i>, observed that the album "proved an ideal showcase for [Chenoweth's] many gifts".<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Among many other solo concerts around the U.S., Chenoweth performed her own concert in 2009 with the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Symphony_Orchestra" title="St. Louis Symphony Orchestra">St. Louis Symphony Orchestra</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Theatre_(St._Louis,_Missouri)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox Theatre (St. Louis, Missouri)">Fox Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010, during her nights off from <i>Promises, Promises</i>, Chenoweth recorded her fourth album, a <a href="/wiki/Country_pop" title="Country pop">country pop</a> CD entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Lessons_Learned" title="Some Lessons Learned">Some Lessons Learned</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Released on September 13, 2011, the album contains songs by <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lady_Antebellum" title="Lady Antebellum">Lady Antebellum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Scott" title="Hillary Scott">Hillary Scott</a>, among others. Chenoweth co-wrote two of the songs.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In advance of the album, Chenoweth released the song "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_Somebody_(Bitch_About)" title="I Want Somebody (Bitch About)">I Want Somebody (Bitch About)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Ben Rimalower, writing in <i>Playbill</i>, thought that the album "may be [Chenoweth's] most accomplished".<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> From the TV show <i>GCB</i>, in 2012, Chenoweth released "Blessed Be the Ties that Bind",<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Jesus_Take_the_Wheel" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Take the Wheel">Jesus Take the Wheel</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Make_Me_an_Instrument_of_Your_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Make Me an Instrument of Your Peace">Prayer of St. Francis</a>" (which was also on <i>Some Lessons Learned</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/This_Little_Light_of_Mine" title="This Little Light of Mine">This Little Light of Mine</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth conducted her first <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Chenoweth_In_Concert" class="mw-redirect" title="Kristin Chenoweth In Concert">U.S. concert tour</a> in the summer of 2012.  The reviewer for BroadwayWorld.com wrote: "Kristin shines on stage."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Less than four months after her July 2012 injury on the set of <i>The Good Wife</i>, Chenoweth returned to the concert stage for a short series of dates in California, where she performed "a sagely programmed 90-minute set, which merged pop, Broadway, gospel and country with perky, unforced-feeling remarks. ... Chenoweth's range, timbre and versatility are in peak form, with astonishing top notes, equalized registers and a delicious ability to variegate attack from number to number."<sup id="cite_ref-fracture_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fracture-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  In 2013, Chenoweth performed at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Opera_House" title="Sydney Opera House">Sydney Opera House</a> as part of an Australian concert tour.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Chenoweth returned to Carnegie Hall with an autobiographical concert, where she sang "as good a rendition of Much More' as we're ever likely to hear".<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie2014_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie2014-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> She also made her London solo concert debut at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, where a reviewer's five-star review noted: "Chenoweth undeniably knows how to engulf a venue, not only with her (sometimes surprisingly) powerful, operatic voice ... but also with her irresistible ... personality ...  that audience was in the palm of her hands for the duration of the evening".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> She joined <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lippa" title="Andrew Lippa">Andrew Lippa</a> in his <a href="/wiki/Oratorio" title="Oratorio">oratorio</a> <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=I_Am_Harvey_Milk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="I Am Harvey Milk (page does not exist)">I Am Harvey Milk</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Avery_Fisher_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Avery Fisher Hall">Avery Fisher Hall</a> on October 6, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Chenoweth released an album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Coming_Home_(Kristin_Chenoweth_album)" title="Coming Home (Kristin Chenoweth album)">Coming Home</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ComingHome_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComingHome-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The album charted at No. 48 on the Billboard 200 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Coming_Home_Tour" title="Coming Home Tour">Coming Home Tour</a> continued into 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth released her next album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Elegance" title="The Art of Elegance">The Art of Elegance</a></i>, in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> which debuted at No. 36 on the <i>Billboard 200</i><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and No. 1 on the Billboard Jazz Albums chart.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> One of the songs on the album, "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Fool_to_Want_You" title="I&#39;m a Fool to Want You">I'm a Fool to Want You</a>" was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for its arrangements.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> She gave a series of concerts at Broadway's <a href="/wiki/Lunt-Fontanne_Theatre" title="Lunt-Fontanne Theatre">Lunt-Fontanne Theatre</a>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Kristin_Chenoweth:_My_Love_Letter_to_Broadway" title="Kristin Chenoweth: My Love Letter to Broadway">My Love Letter to Broadway</a></i>, in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, she gave a concert at the <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a>, where she "put on a spectacular show and simultaneously formed a heartfelt connection with her fans."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth plans to release a new album, <i>For the Girls</i>, on September 27, 2019, to feature covers of songs by female performers from various genres that have influenced her. She is collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson" title="Jennifer Hudson">Jennifer Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a> on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_events_and_appearances">Special events and appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special events and appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Chenoweth and the cast of the Broadway musical <i>Wicked</i> performed the song "One Short Day" in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy&#39;s Thanksgiving Day Parade">Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In the 2005 Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade, Chenoweth performed the song "Oklahoma" while riding aboard the "Oklahoma Rising" float. The float was making the first of three annual appearances commemorating the state of Oklahoma's statehood centennial in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> She was the star performer of the opening ceremony of the 2007 Tournament of Roses Parade. She sang "Our Good Nature", an original composition written to coincide with the Oklahoma centennial celebration and the theme of the parade.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In the 2008 Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade, she performed the song "The Christmas Waltz" from her "A Lovely Way to Spend Christmas" album while riding aboard the "Care Bears Winter Fun-Derland" float.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She sang with <a href="/wiki/Il_Divo" title="Il Divo">Il Divo</a> as part of Il Divo's Christmas Tour on <span class="nowrap">December 15</span>, 16 and 17, 2009 in New York City and <span class="nowrap">December 18</span> in Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> She has sung the <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">U.S. national anthem</a> at various sporting events, including the 2010 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> home opener,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Candlestick_Park" title="Candlestick Park">Candlestick Park</a> for the <a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NFL_playoffs" title="2011–12 NFL playoffs">NFC Conference Championship</a> on January 22, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> at the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Cardinals" title="Arizona Cardinals">Arizona Cardinals</a>' season opener in 2016 and their game at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Phoenix_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Phoenix Stadium">University of Phoenix Stadium</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> on November 9, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2010, Chenoweth hosted the <a href="/wiki/15th_Critics%27_Choice_Awards" title="15th Critics&#39; Choice Awards">15th Annual Broadcast Film Critics Association Awards</a> on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Chenoweth co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/Oscars_Red_Carpet_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscars Red Carpet Live">Oscars Red Carpet Live</a> immediately prior to the <a href="/wiki/85th_Academy_Awards" title="85th Academy Awards">85th Academy Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and also sang the closing number of the ceremony, "Here's to the Losers", with host <a href="/wiki/Seth_MacFarlane" title="Seth MacFarlane">Seth MacFarlane</a>, in which, paraphrasing the original <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a> song, the two poked genial fun at nominees who had not received awards.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>  Chenoweth was the solo performer in the <a href="/wiki/Live_from_Lincoln_Center" title="Live from Lincoln Center">Live from Lincoln Center</a> feature "The Dames of Broadway... All of 'Em!!!"<sup id="cite_ref-Rimalower_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rimalower-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In July, she hosted the fifth <a href="/wiki/Just_For_Laughs" class="mw-redirect" title="Just For Laughs">Just For Laughs</a> gala in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> She also appeared in the 2013 Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade performing the song "<a href="/wiki/Theme_from_New_York,_New_York" title="Theme from New York, New York">New York, New York</a>" while riding aboard <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">Royal Caribbean</a>'s "A World at Sea" float.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, she co-hosted the Tony Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> She appeared as a guest with Andrea Bocelli on some of his 2017–2018 American tour stops.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> In December 2018, Chenoweth was the guest artist for the <a href="/wiki/The_Tabernacle_Choir_at_Temple_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="The Tabernacle Choir at Temple Square">Tabernacle Choir at Temple Square</a>'s Christmas Concert in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, Utah.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth,_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg/220px-Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg/330px-Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg/440px-Kristin_Chenoweth%2C_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1430" data-file-height="2144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristin_Chenoweth,_Yankees_Home_Opener_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chenoweth sang the U.S. national anthem for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankee" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Yankee">Yankees</a>' Home Opener, 2010</div></div></div>
<p>In 2009, Chenoweth wrote a memoir entitled <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Bit_Wicked" title="A Little Bit Wicked">A Little Bit Wicked: Life, Love, and Faith in Stages</a></i>, describing her life and career, including her adoption, her turn in <i>Wicked</i> and her time in Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth has spoken publicly about her religious faith; she describes herself as a "non-judgmental, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Christianity" title="Liberal Christianity">liberal Christian</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i>The New York Times</i>, when Chenoweth "assured her theater fans that she supports gay rights, her Christian base was outraged; she was disinvited from performing at a Women of Faith conference in <span class="nowrap">September 2005</span>".<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth released an album in <span class="nowrap">April 2005</span>, <i><a href="/wiki/As_I_Am_(Kristin_Chenoweth_album)" title="As I Am (Kristin Chenoweth album)">As I Am</a></i>, a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">hymns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Christian_music" title="Contemporary Christian music">contemporary Christian music</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary_music" title="Adult contemporary music">adult contemporary</a> arrangements. To promote the album, she made an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_700_Club" title="The 700 Club">The 700 Club</a></i> which upset some of her gay fans.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> She later said she thought that the "<a href="/wiki/Pat_Robertson" title="Pat Robertson">Pat Robertsons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Falwell" title="Jerry Falwell">Jerry Falwells</a> of the world are scary" and that she regretted appearing on the show.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth has dated several men in Hollywood, including producer <a href="/wiki/Dana_Brunetti" title="Dana Brunetti">Dana Brunetti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> actors <a href="/wiki/Seth_Green" title="Seth Green">Seth Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lane_Garrison" title="Lane Garrison">Lane Garrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Kudisch" title="Marc Kudisch">Marc Kudisch</a> (to whom she was engaged from 1998 to 2001),<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and producer/writer <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sorkin" title="Aaron Sorkin">Aaron Sorkin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In Sorkin's <i><a href="/wiki/Studio_60_on_the_Sunset_Strip" title="Studio 60 on the Sunset Strip">Studio 60 on the Sunset Strip</a></i>, the character of the Christian <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Hayes" title="Harriet Hayes">Harriet Hayes</a> bears significant resemblances to Chenoweth, and the relationship between Hayes and "East coast liberal Jewish atheist" (Hayes' description) <a href="/wiki/Matt_Albie" class="mw-redirect" title="Matt Albie">Matt Albie</a> is modeled after that of Chenoweth and Sorkin. For example, Chenoweth's decision to appear on <i>The 700 Club</i> and her falling out with Women of Faith were depicted with the Hayes character.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chenoweth suffers from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9ni%C3%A8re%27s_disease" title="Ménière&#39;s disease">Ménière's disease</a>, an inner-ear disorder that can cause vertigo, headaches and nausea, among other symptoms. She has said that during some performances she has had to lean on her co-stars to keep her balance and that it has caused her to miss performances.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR2009_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2010, Chenoweth wrote in response to <a href="/wiki/Newsweek_gay_actor_controversy" title="Newsweek gay actor controversy">an article in <i>Newsweek</i></a> by Ramin Setoodeh, an openly gay writer. Setoodeh thought that her Tony-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Promises,_Promises_(musical)" title="Promises, Promises (musical)">Promises, Promises</a></i> co-star, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Hayes_(actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Hayes (actor)">Sean Hayes</a>, "comes off as wooden and insincere" in playing the straight character Chuck, and that <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Groff" title="Jonathan Groff">Jonathan Groff</a> has a similar credibility problem in the TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>. He questioned whether any openly gay actor could acceptably portray a straight character.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth called the article "horrendously homophobic" and criticized Setoodeh's view as rationalizing "the same kind of bullying" that gay youths face in high school. Chenoweth argued that audiences "come to the theater to go on a journey" and do not care about an actor's sexual orientation.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The story was picked up by major media including <i>The New York Times</i><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the <i>Los Angeles Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Credits">Credits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Credits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Chenoweth_credits" title="Kristin Chenoweth credits">Kristin Chenoweth credits</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kristin_Chenoweth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Chenoweth was awarded an honorary doctorate in Performing Arts from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_School_of_the_Arts" title="University of North Carolina School of the Arts">University of North Carolina School of the Arts</a> in 2009, where she was the commencement speaker.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Oklahoma City University, where she received her undergraduate and master's degrees, awarded her an honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Humane_Letters" title="Doctor of Humane Letters">Doctor of Humane Letters</a> degree in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Allen_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Chenoweth was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, she won the <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Vanguard_Award" title="GLAAD Vanguard Award">GLAAD Vanguard Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, the Broken Arrow Performing Arts Center named its theatre the Kristin Chenoweth Theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Chenoweth received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in 2015 for Live Performance.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodWalk_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodWalk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, she was inducted as an honorary member of the <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Iota" title="Sigma Alpha Iota">Sigma Alpha Iota</a> music fraternity's Sigma Theta chapter at <a href="/wiki/Eastman_School_of_Music" title="Eastman School of Music">Eastman School of Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
